From the 15th to 18th centuries, when the disintegrating khanates of the [Golden Horde](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Horde "Golden Horde") were conquered by Russia, [Tatars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatars "Crimean Tatars") from the [Crimean Khanate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Khanate "Crimean Khanate") frequently [raided](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean-Nogai_raids_into_East_Slavic_lands "Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands") Eastern Slavic lands to [capture slaves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire "Slavery in the Ottoman Empire").[^181] Further east, the [Nogai Horde](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nogai_Horde "Nogai Horde") and [Kazakh Khanate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakh_Khanate "Kazakh Khanate") frequently raided the Slavic-speaking areas of contemporary Russia and Ukraine for hundreds of years, until the Russian expansion and conquest of most of northern Eurasia (i.e. Eastern Europe, Central Asia and Siberia).

The Renaissance and the [New Monarchs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Monarchs "New Monarchs") marked the start of an Age of Discovery, a period of exploration, invention and scientific development.[^182] Important figures of the [Scientific Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_Revolution "Scientific Revolution") during the 16th and 17th centuries included [Copernicus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copernicus "Copernicus"), [Kepler](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kepler "Kepler"), [Galileo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo "Galileo"), and [Isaac Newton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Newton "Isaac Newton").[^183] According to Peter Barrett, "It is widely accepted that 'modern science' arose in the Europe of the 17th century (towards the end of the Renaissance), introducing a new understanding of the natural world." [^154]

The national boundaries within Europe set by the [Congress of Vienna](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna "Congress of Vienna")

The [Seven Years' War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War "Seven Years' War") brought to an end the ["Old System" of alliances in Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Alliance_\(League_of_Augsburg\) "Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)"). Consequently, when the [American Revolutionary War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") turned into a global war between 1778 and 1783, Britain found itself opposed by a strong coalition of European powers, and lacking any substantial ally.[^184]

The Age of Enlightenment was a powerful intellectual movement during the 18th century promoting scientific and reason-based thoughts.[^185] [^186] [^187] Discontent with the aristocracy and clergy's monopoly on political power in France resulted in the French Revolution, and the establishment of the [First Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_First_Republic "French First Republic") as a result of which the monarchy and many of the nobility perished during the initial [reign of terror](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reign_of_Terror "Reign of Terror").[^188] [Napoleon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon "Napoleon") Bonaparte rose to power in the aftermath of the French Revolution, and established the [First French Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_French_Empire "First French Empire") that, during the [Napoleonic Wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars"), grew to encompass large parts of Europe before collapsing in 1815 with the [Battle of Waterloo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo "Battle of Waterloo").[^189] [^190] [Napoleonic rule](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Empire "Napoleonic Empire") resulted in the further dissemination of the ideals of the French Revolution, including that of the [nation state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state"), as well as the widespread adoption of the French models of [administration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centralised_government "Centralised government"), [law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_code "Napoleonic code") and [education](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_France "Education in France").[^191] [^192] [^193] The [Congress of Vienna](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna "Congress of Vienna"), convened after Napoleon's downfall, established a new [balance of power](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balance_of_power_\(international_relations\) "Balance of power (international relations)") in Europe centred on the five " [great powers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_power "Great power") ": the UK, France, [Prussia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussia "Prussia"), [Austria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_Empire "Austrian Empire"), and Russia.[^194] This balance would remain in place until the [Revolutions of 1848](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848 "Revolutions of 1848"), during which liberal uprisings affected all of Europe except for Russia and the UK. These revolutions were eventually put down by conservative elements and few reforms resulted.[^195] The year 1859 saw the unification of Romania, as a nation state, from smaller principalities. In 1867, the [Austro-Hungarian empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_empire "Austro-Hungarian empire") was [formed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ausgleich "Ausgleich"); 1871 saw the unifications of both [Italy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_unification "Italian unification") and [Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unification_of_Germany "Unification of Germany") as nation-states from smaller principalities.[^196]

In parallel, the [Eastern Question](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Question "Eastern Question") grew more complex ever since the Ottoman defeat in the [Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1768%E2%80%931774\) "Russo-Turkish War (1768–1774)"). As the dissolution of the Ottoman Empire seemed imminent, the [Great Powers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Power "Great Power") struggled to safeguard their strategic and commercial interests in the Ottoman domains. The [Russian Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") stood to benefit from the decline, whereas the [Habsburg Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg_monarchy "Habsburg monarchy") and Britain perceived the preservation of the Ottoman Empire to be in their best interests. Meanwhile, the [Serbian Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_Revolution "Serbian Revolution") (1804) and [Greek War of Independence](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence "Greek War of Independence") (1821) marked the beginning of the end of Ottoman rule in the [Balkans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans"), which ended with the [Balkan Wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Balkan Wars") in 1912–1913.[^197] Formal recognition of the *de facto* independent principalities of [Montenegro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montenegro "Montenegro"), [Serbia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia "Principality of Serbia") and [Romania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania "Romania") ensued at the [Congress of Berlin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin "Congress of Berlin") in 1878.

Marshall's [Temple Works](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Works "Temple Works") (1840); the [Industrial Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution "Industrial Revolution") started in [Great Britain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain "Kingdom of Great Britain").

The [Industrial Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution "Industrial Revolution") started in [Great Britain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain "Kingdom of Great Britain") in the last part of the 18th century and spread throughout Europe. The invention and implementation of new technologies resulted in rapid urban growth, mass employment and the rise of a new working class.[^198] Reforms in social and economic spheres followed, including the [first laws](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Factory_Acts "Factory Acts") on [child labour](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_labour "Child labour"), the legalisation of [trade unions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_union "Trade union"),[^199] and the [abolition of slavery](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom "Abolitionism in the United Kingdom").[^200] In Britain, the [Public Health Act of 1875](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_Health_Act_of_1875 "Public Health Act of 1875") was passed, which significantly improved living conditions in many British cities.[^201] Europe's population increased from about 100 million in 1700 to 400 million by 1900.[^202] The last major famine recorded in Western Europe, the [Great Famine of Ireland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Famine_\(Ireland\) "Great Famine (Ireland)"), caused death and mass emigration of millions of Irish people.[^203] In the 19th century, 70 million people left Europe in migrations to various European colonies abroad and to the United States.[^204] The industrial revolution also led to large population growth, and the [share of the world population living in Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_the_world#Shares_of_world_population,_AD_1%E2%80%931998_\(%_of_world_total\) "Demographics of the world") reached a peak of slightly above 25% around the year 1913.[^205] <sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-World_Population_Growth,_1950%E2%80%932050-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup>

Map of European [colonial empires](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_empire "Colonial empire") throughout the world in 1914

Two world wars and an economic depression dominated the first half of the 20th century. The First World War was fought between 1914 and 1918. It started when [Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria "Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria") was assassinated by the [Yugoslav nationalist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_nationalism "Yugoslav nationalism") [^207] [Gavrilo Princip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavrilo_Princip "Gavrilo Princip").[^208] Most European nations were drawn into the war, which was fought between the [Entente Powers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entente_Powers "Entente Powers") ([France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Third_Republic "French Third Republic"), [Belgium](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belgium "Belgium"), [Serbia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbia "Serbia"), Portugal, [Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire"), the United Kingdom, and later [Italy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy "Italy"), [Greece](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece "Greece"), [Romania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania "Romania"), and the United States) and the [Central Powers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers") ([Austria-Hungary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary "Austria-Hungary"), [Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Empire "German Empire"), [Bulgaria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria "Bulgaria"), and the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire")). The war left more than 16 million civilians and military dead.[^209] Over 60 million European soldiers were mobilised from 1914 to 1918.[^210]

Map depicting the military alliances of the [First World War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_World_War "First World War") in 1914–1918

Russia was plunged into the [Russian Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution"), which threw down the [Tsarist monarchy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") and replaced it with the [communist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist "Communist") [Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"),[^211] leading also to the independence of many former [Russian governorates](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governorate_\(Russia\) "Governorate (Russia)"), such as [Finland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland "Finland"), [Estonia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), [Latvia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvia "Latvia") and [Lithuania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania"), as new European countries.[^212] [Austria-Hungary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary "Austria-Hungary") and the Ottoman Empire collapsed and broke up into separate nations, and many other nations had their borders redrawn. The [Treaty of Versailles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles "Treaty of Versailles"), which officially ended the First World War in 1919, was harsh towards Germany, upon whom it placed full responsibility for the war and imposed heavy sanctions.[^213] Excess deaths in Russia over the course of the First World War and the [Russian Civil War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War") (including the postwar [famine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921 "Russian famine of 1921")) amounted to a combined total of 18 million.[^214] In 1932–1933, under [Stalin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalin "Stalin") 's leadership, confiscations of grain by the Soviet authorities contributed to the [second Soviet famine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932-1933 "Soviet famine of 1932-1933") which caused millions of deaths;[^215] surviving [kulaks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kulak "Kulak") were persecuted and many sent to [Gulags](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag") to do [forced labour](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unfree_labour "Unfree labour"). Stalin was also responsible for the [Great Purge](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge") of 1937–38 in which the [NKVD](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") executed 681,692 people;[^216] millions of people were [deported and exiled](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union "Population transfer in the Soviet Union") to remote areas of the Soviet Union.[^217]

[Serbian war efforts](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian_Campaign_of_World_War_I "Serbian Campaign of World War I") (1914–1918) cost the country one quarter of its population.[^218] [^219] [^220] [^221] [^222]

[Nazi Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") began the devastating Second World War in Europe by its leader, [Adolf Hitler](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler"). Here Hitler, on the right, with his closest ally, the Italian dictator [Benito Mussolini](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini"), in 1940.

The [social revolutions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_revolution "Social revolution") sweeping through Russia also affected other European nations following [The Great War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Great_War "The Great War"): in 1919, with the [Weimar Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weimar_Republic "Weimar Republic") in Germany and the [First Austrian Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Austrian_Republic "First Austrian Republic"); in 1922, with [Mussolini](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini") 's one-party [fascist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism") government in the [Kingdom of Italy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy "Kingdom of Italy") and in [Atatürk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk "Atatürk") 's [Turkish Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey"), adopting the Western alphabet and state [secularism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secularism "Secularism"). Economic instability, caused in part by debts incurred in the First World War and 'loans' to Germany played havoc in Europe in the late 1920s and 1930s. This, and the [Wall Street crash of 1929](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_crash_of_1929 "Wall Street crash of 1929"), brought about the worldwide [Great Depression](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression"). Helped by the economic crisis, social instability and the threat of communism, [fascist movements](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism") developed throughout Europe placing [Adolf Hitler](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") in power of what became [Nazi Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany").[^223] [^224]

In 1933, Hitler became the leader of Germany and began to work towards his goal of building Greater Germany. Germany re-expanded and took back the [Saarland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saarland "Saarland") and [Rhineland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhineland "Rhineland") in 1935 and 1936. In 1938, [Austria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria "Austria") became a part of Germany following the [Anschluss](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anschluss "Anschluss"). Following the [Munich Agreement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_Agreement "Munich Agreement") signed by Germany, France, the United Kingdom, and Italy, later in 1938 Germany annexed the [Sudetenland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudetenland "Sudetenland"), which was a part of [Czechoslovakia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia "Czechoslovakia") inhabited by ethnic Germans. In early 1939, the remainder of Czechoslovakia was split into the [Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia "Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia"), controlled by Germany and the [Slovak Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slovak_Republic_\(1939%E2%80%931945\) "Slovak Republic (1939–1945)"). At the time, the United Kingdom and France preferred a policy of [appeasement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appeasement "Appeasement").

With tensions mounting between Germany and [Poland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic") over the future of [Danzig](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk "Gdańsk"), the Germans turned to the Soviets and signed the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact"), which allowed the Soviets to invade the Baltic states and parts of Poland and Romania. Germany [invaded Poland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland "Invasion of Poland") on 1 September 1939, prompting France and the United Kingdom to declare war on Germany on 3 September, opening the [European Theatre of the Second World War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Theatre_of_World_War_II "European Theatre of World War II").[^225] [^226] [^227] The [Soviet invasion of Poland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland "Soviet invasion of Poland") started on 17 September and Poland fell soon thereafter. On 24 September, the Soviet Union attacked the [Baltic countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_\(1940\) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)") and, on 30 November, Finland, the latter of which was followed by the devastating [Winter War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_War "Winter War") for the Red Army.[^228] The British hoped to land at [Narvik](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Narvik "Battles of Narvik") and send troops to aid Finland, but their primary objective in the landing was to encircle Germany and cut the Germans off from Scandinavian resources. Around the same time, Germany moved troops into Denmark. The [Phoney War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoney_War "Phoney War") continued.

In May 1940, Germany [attacked France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_France "Battle of France") through the Low Countries. France capitulated in June 1940. By August, Germany had begun a [bombing offensive against the United Kingdom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Britain "Battle of Britain") but failed to convince the Britons to give up.[^229] In 1941, Germany invaded the Soviet Union in [Operation Barbarossa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa").[^230] On 7 December 1941 [Japan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan") 's [attack on Pearl Harbor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") drew the United States into the conflict as allies of the [British Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire"), and other [allied](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") forces.[^231] [^232]

The " [Big Three](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") " at the [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") in 1945; seated (from the left): [Winston Churchill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill"), [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") and [Joseph Stalin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin")

After the staggering [Battle of Stalingrad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad") in 1943, the German offensive in the Soviet Union turned into a continual fallback. The [Battle of Kursk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk "Battle of Kursk"), which involved the largest [tank battle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Prokhorovka "Battle of Prokhorovka") in history, was the last major German offensive on the [Eastern Front](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_\(World_War_II\) "Eastern Front (World War II)"). In June 1944, British and American forces invaded France in the [D-Day landings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normandy_landings "Normandy landings"), opening a new front against Germany. Berlin finally [fell in 1945](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin "Battle of Berlin"), ending the Second World War in Europe. The war was the largest and most destructive in human history, with [60 million dead across the world](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties "World War II casualties").[^233] More than 40 million people in Europe had died as a result of the Second World War,[^234] including between 11 and 17 million people who perished during [the Holocaust](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust").[^235] The Soviet Union [lost around 27 million people](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union") (mostly civilians) during the war, about half of all Second World War casualties.[^236] By the end of the Second World War, Europe had more than 40 million [refugees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugee "Refugee").[^237] [^238] [^239] Several [post-war expulsions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_evacuation_and_expulsion "World War II evacuation and expulsion") in Central and Eastern Europe displaced a total of about 20 million people.[^240]

The First World War, and especially the Second World War, diminished the eminence of Western Europe in world affairs. After the Second World War the map of Europe was redrawn at the [Yalta Conference](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalta_Conference "Yalta Conference") and divided into two blocs, the Western countries and the communist Eastern bloc, separated by what was later called by [Winston Churchill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill") an " [Iron Curtain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Curtain "Iron Curtain") ". The United States and Western Europe established the [NATO](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") alliance and, later, the Soviet Union and Central Europe established the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact").[^241] Particular hot spots after the Second World War were [Berlin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin "Berlin") and [Trieste](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste"), whereby the [Free Territory of Trieste](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_Territory_of_Trieste "Free Territory of Trieste"), founded in 1947 with the UN, was dissolved in 1954 and 1975, respectively. The [Berlin blockade](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_blockade "Berlin blockade") in 1948 and 1949 and the construction of the [Berlin Wall](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Wall "Berlin Wall") in 1961 were one of the great international crises of the [Cold War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War").[^242] [^243] [^244]

The two new [superpowers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower"), the United States and the Soviet Union, became locked in a fifty-year-long Cold War, centred on [nuclear proliferation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation "Nuclear proliferation"). At the same time [decolonisation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonisation "Decolonisation"), which had already started after the First World War, gradually resulted in the independence of most of the European colonies in Asia and Africa.[^36]

[Flag of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Europe "Flag of Europe"), adopted by the [Council of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe") in 1955 as the flag for the whole of Europe [^245]

In the 1980s the [reforms](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glasnost "Glasnost") of [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev") and the [Solidarity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solidarity_\(Polish_trade_union\) "Solidarity (Polish trade union)") movement in Poland weakened the previously rigid communist system. The opening of the [Iron Curtain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Curtain "Iron Curtain") at the [Pan-European Picnic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-European_Picnic "Pan-European Picnic") then set in motion a peaceful chain reaction, at the end of which the [Eastern bloc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_bloc "Eastern bloc"), the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact") and other [communist states collapsed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989"), and the Cold War ended.[^246] [^247] [^248] Germany was reunited, after the symbolic [fall of the Berlin Wall](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Wall#Fall_of_the_Wall "Berlin Wall") in 1989 and the maps of Central and Eastern Europe were redrawn once more.[^249] This made old previously interrupted cultural and economic relationships possible, and previously isolated cities such as [Berlin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin "Berlin"), [Prague](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prague "Prague"), [Vienna](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna "Vienna"), [Budapest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budapest "Budapest") and [Trieste](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste") were now again in the centre of Europe.[^223] [^250] [^251] [^252]

[European integration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_integration "European integration") also grew after the Second World War. In 1949 the [Council of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe") was founded, following a speech by Sir [Winston Churchill](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winston_Churchill "Winston Churchill"), with the idea of unifying Europe [^37] to achieve common goals. It includes all European states except for [Belarus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus"), Russia,[^253] and [Vatican City](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vatican_City "Vatican City"). The [Treaty of Rome](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome "Treaty of Rome") in 1957 established the [European Economic Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Economic_Community "European Economic Community") between six Western European states with the goal of a unified economic policy and common market.[^254] In 1967 the EEC, [European Coal and Steel Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community "European Coal and Steel Community"), and [Euratom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euratom "Euratom") formed the [European Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Community "European Community"), which in 1993 became the [European Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union"). The EU established [a parliament](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament"), [a court](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice "European Court of Justice") and [a central bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Central_Bank "European Central Bank"), and introduced the [euro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro "Euro") as a unified currency.[^255] Between 2004 and 2013, more Central European countries began joining, [expanding the EU](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union "Enlargement of the European Union") to 28 European countries and once more making Europe a major economical and political centre of power.[^256] However, the United Kingdom withdrew from the EU on 31 January 2020, as a result of a [June 2016 referendum on EU membership](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum "2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum").[^257] The [Russo-Ukrainian War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War"), which has been ongoing since 2014, steeply escalated when Russia launched [a full-scale invasion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine") of [Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") on 24 February 2022, marking the largest humanitarian and refugee crisis in Europe since the Second World War [^258] and the [Yugoslav Wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars "Yugoslav Wars").[^259]

## Geography

General topographic map of Europe showing physical, political and population characteristics, as per 2024

Europe makes up the western fifth of the [Eurasian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") landmass.[^48] It has a higher ratio of coast to landmass than any other continent or subcontinent.[^260] Its maritime borders consist of the Arctic Ocean to the north, the Atlantic Ocean to the west and the Mediterranean, Black and Caspian Seas to the south.[^261] Land relief in Europe shows great variation within relatively small areas. The southern regions are more mountainous, while moving north the terrain descends from the high [Alps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alps "Alps"), [Pyrenees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyrenees "Pyrenees") and [Carpathians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathians "Carpathians"), through hilly uplands, into broad, low northern plains, which are vast in the east. This extended lowland is known as the [Great European Plain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_European_Plain "Great European Plain") and at its heart lies the [North German Plain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_German_Plain "North German Plain"). An arc of uplands also exists along the north-western seaboard, which begins in the western parts of the islands of Britain and Ireland, and then continues along the mountainous, [fjord](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fjord "Fjord") -cut spine of Norway.

This description is simplified. Subregions such as the [Iberian Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula "Iberian Peninsula") and the [Italian Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Peninsula "Italian Peninsula") contain their own complex features, as does mainland Central Europe itself, where the relief contains many plateaus, river valleys and basins that complicate the general trend. Sub-regions like [Iceland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iceland "Iceland"), Britain and Ireland are special cases. The former is a land unto itself in the northern ocean that is counted as part of Europe, while the latter are upland areas that were once joined to the mainland until [rising sea levels](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_level_rise "Sea level rise") cut them off.

The [largest European lakes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_lakes_of_Europe "List of largest lakes of Europe") are located in the north of the continent. The [Volga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga "Volga") and [Danube](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danube "Danube") are the two longest [rivers of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Europe "List of rivers of Europe"). Europe's largest [waterfall](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterfall "Waterfall") (by [flow rate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_waterfalls_by_flow_rate "List of waterfalls by flow rate")) are the [Rhine Falls](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhine_Falls "Rhine Falls") on the [Rhine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhine "Rhine").

### Climate

[Biomes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biome "Biome") of Europe and surrounding regions:  
[tundra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra "Tundra") [alpine tundra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_tundra "Alpine tundra") [taiga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiga "Taiga") [montane forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montane_forest "Montane forest")  
[temperate broadleaf forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_forest "Temperate broadleaf forest") [mediterranean forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_forest "Mediterranean forest") [temperate steppe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_steppe "Temperate steppe") [dry steppe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dry_steppe "Dry steppe")

Europe lies mainly in the [temperate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate "Temperate") climate zone of the northern hemisphere, where the [prevailing wind direction is from the west](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prevailing_westerlies "Prevailing westerlies"). The climate is milder in comparison to other areas of the same latitude around the globe due to the influence of the [Gulf Stream](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Stream "Gulf Stream"), an ocean current which carries warm water from the [Gulf of Mexico](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico "Gulf of Mexico") across the [Atlantic Ocean](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") to Europe.[^262] The Gulf Stream is nicknamed "Europe's central heating", because it makes Europe's climate warmer and wetter than it would otherwise be. The Gulf Stream not only carries warm water to Europe's coast but also warms up the prevailing westerly winds that blow across the continent from the Atlantic Ocean.

Therefore, the average temperature throughout the year of [Aveiro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal "Aveiro, Portugal") is 16 °C (61 °F), while it is only 13 °C (55 °F) in [New York City](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City") which is almost on the same latitude, bordering the same ocean. Berlin, Germany; Calgary, Canada; and Irkutsk, in far south-eastern Russia, lie on around the same latitude; January temperatures in Berlin average around 8 °C (14 °F) higher than those in Calgary and they are almost 22 °C (40 °F) higher than average temperatures in Irkutsk.[^262]

The large water masses of the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea"), which equalise the temperatures on an annual and daily average, are also of particular importance. The water of the Mediterranean extends from the [Sahara desert](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahara_desert "Sahara desert") to the Alpine arc in its northernmost part of the [Adriatic Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea") near [Trieste](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste").[^263]

In general, Europe is not just colder towards the north compared to the south, but it also gets colder from the west towards the east. The climate is more oceanic in the west and less so in the east. This can be illustrated by the following table of average temperatures at locations roughly following the 64th, 60th, 55th, 50th, 45th and 40th [latitudes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latitudes "Latitudes"). None of them is located at high altitude; most of them are close to the sea.

[Köppen-Geiger climate classification](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") map for Europe [^264]

[^265] The average temperatures for the coldest month, as well as the annual average temperatures, drop from the west to the east. For instance, Edinburgh is warmer than Belgrade during the coldest month of the year, although Belgrade is around 10° of latitude farther south.

### Climate change

Increase of average yearly temperature (2000–2017) above the 20th century average in selected cities in Europe [^266]

[Climate change](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") has resulted in an increase in temperature of 2.3 °C (4.14 °F) (2022) in Europe compared to pre-industrial levels. Europe is the fastest warming continent in the world.[^267] [Europe's climate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_Europe "Climate of Europe") is getting warmer due to [anthropogenic activity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropogenic_greenhouse_gas "Anthropogenic greenhouse gas"). According to international climate experts, global temperature rise should not exceed 2 [°C](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C2%B0C "°C") to prevent the most dangerous [consequences of climate change](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change "Effects of climate change"); without reduction in [greenhouse gas emissions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions "Greenhouse gas emissions"), this could happen before 2050.[^268] [^269] [Climate change](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") has implications for all regions of Europe, with the extent and nature of effects varying across the continent. Effects on European countries include warmer weather and increasing frequency and intensity of [extreme weather](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_weather "Extreme weather") such as [heat waves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_wave "Heat wave"), bringing [health risks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_human_health "Effects of climate change on human health") and effects on ecosystems. European countries are major contributors to global greenhouse gas emissions, although the [European Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") and governments of several countries have outlined plans to implement [climate change mitigation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation "Climate change mitigation") and an [energy transition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_transition "Energy transition") in the 21st century, the [European Green Deal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Green_Deal "European Green Deal") being one of these.

### Geology

Surficial geology of Europe

The geological history of Europe traces back to the formation of the [Baltic Shield](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Shield "Baltic Shield") (Fennoscandia) and the [Sarmatian craton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarmatian_craton "Sarmatian craton"), both around 2.25 billion years ago, followed by the [Volgo–Uralia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volgo%E2%80%93Uralia "Volgo–Uralia") shield, the three together leading to the [East European craton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_European_craton "East European craton") (≈ [Baltica](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltica "Baltica")) which became a part of the [supercontinent](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercontinent "Supercontinent") [Columbia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbia_\(supercontinent\) "Columbia (supercontinent)"). Around 1.1 billion years ago, Baltica and Arctica (as part of the [Laurentia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurentia "Laurentia") block) became joined to [Rodinia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rodinia "Rodinia"), later resplitting around 550 million years ago to reform as Baltica. Around 440 million years ago [Euramerica](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euramerica "Euramerica") was formed from Baltica and Laurentia; a further joining with [Gondwana](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gondwana "Gondwana") then leading to the formation of [Pangea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pangea "Pangea"). Around 190 million years ago, Gondwana and [Laurasia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laurasia "Laurasia") split apart due to the widening of the Atlantic Ocean. Finally and very soon afterwards, Laurasia itself split up again, into Laurentia (North America) and the Eurasian continent. The land connection between the two persisted for a considerable time, via [Greenland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenland "Greenland"), leading to interchange of animal species. From around 50 million years ago, rising and falling sea levels have determined the actual shape of Europe and its connections with continents such as Asia. Europe's present shape dates to the [late Tertiary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Tertiary "Late Tertiary") period about five million years ago.<sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup>

The geology of Europe is hugely varied and complex and gives rise to the wide variety of landscapes found across the continent, from the [Scottish Highlands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scottish_Highlands "Scottish Highlands") to the rolling [plains](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plain "Plain") of Hungary.[^271] Europe's most significant feature is the dichotomy between highland and mountainous [Southern Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Europe "Southern Europe") and a vast, partially underwater, northern plain ranging from Ireland in the west to the [Ural Mountains](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ural_Mountains "Ural Mountains") in the east. These two halves are separated by the mountain chains of the [Pyrenees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyrenees "Pyrenees") and [Alps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alps "Alps") / [Carpathians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains "Carpathian Mountains"). The northern plains are delimited in the west by the [Scandinavian Mountains](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scandinavian_Mountains "Scandinavian Mountains") and the mountainous parts of the British Isles. Major shallow water bodies submerging parts of the northern plains are the [Celtic Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtic_Sea "Celtic Sea"), the [North Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Sea "North Sea"), the [Baltic Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") complex and [Barents Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barents_Sea "Barents Sea").

The northern plain contains the old geological continent of [Baltica](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltica "Baltica") and so may be regarded geologically as the "main continent", while peripheral highlands and mountainous regions in the south and west constitute fragments from various other geological continents. Most of the older geology of western Europe existed as part of the ancient [microcontinent](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microcontinent "Microcontinent") [Avalonia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avalonia "Avalonia").

### Flora

Land use map of Europe with arable farmland (yellow), forest (dark green), pasture (light green) and tundra, or bogs, in the north (dark yellow)

Having lived side by side with agricultural peoples for millennia, Europe's animals and plants have been profoundly affected by the presence and activities of humans. With the exception of [Fennoscandia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fennoscandia "Fennoscandia") and northern Russia, few areas of untouched wilderness are currently found in Europe, except for various [national parks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_park "National park").

The main natural vegetation cover in Europe is mixed [forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest "Forest"). The conditions for growth are very favourable. In the north, the [Gulf Stream](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Stream "Gulf Stream") and [North Atlantic Drift](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Atlantic_Current "North Atlantic Current") warm the continent. Southern Europe has a warm but mild climate. There are frequent summer droughts in this region. Mountain ridges also affect the conditions. Some of these, such as the [Alps](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alps "Alps") and the [Pyrenees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyrenees "Pyrenees"), are oriented east–west and allow the wind to carry large masses of water from the ocean in the interior. Others are oriented south–north ([Scandinavian Mountains](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scandinavian_Mountains "Scandinavian Mountains"), [Dinarides](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dinaric_Alps "Dinaric Alps"), [Carpathians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains "Carpathian Mountains"), [Apennines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apennine_Mountains "Apennine Mountains")) and because the rain falls primarily on the side of mountains that is oriented towards the sea, forests grow well on this side, while on the other side, the conditions are much less favourable. Few corners of mainland Europe have not been grazed by [livestock](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livestock "Livestock") at some point in time, and the cutting down of the preagricultural forest habitat caused disruption to the original plant and animal ecosystems.

Floristic regions of Europe and neighbouring areas, according to Wolfgang Frey and Rainer Lösch

Possibly 80 to 90 percent of Europe was once covered by forest.[^272] It stretched from the Mediterranean Sea to the Arctic Ocean. Although over half of Europe's original forests disappeared through the centuries of [deforestation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation "Deforestation"), Europe still has over one quarter of its land area as forest, such as the [broadleaf and mixed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forest "Temperate broadleaf and mixed forest") forests, [taiga](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiga "Taiga") of Scandinavia and Russia, mixed [rainforests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rainforest "Rainforest") of the Caucasus and the [Cork oak](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cork_oak "Cork oak") forests in the western Mediterranean. During recent times, deforestation has been slowed and many trees have been planted. However, in many cases monoculture [plantations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plantation "Plantation") of [conifers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinophyta "Pinophyta") have replaced the original mixed natural forest, because these grow quicker. The plantations now cover vast areas of land, but offer poorer habitats for many European forest dwelling species which require a mixture of tree species and diverse forest structure. The amount of natural forest in Western Europe is just 2–3% or less, while in its Western Russia its 5–10%. The European country with the [smallest percentage of forested area](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_forest_area "List of countries by forest area") is [Iceland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iceland "Iceland") (1%), while the most forested country is Finland (77%).[^273]

In temperate Europe, mixed forest with both [broadleaf](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant "Flowering plant") and coniferous trees dominate. The most important species in central and western Europe are [beech](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beech "Beech") and [oak](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oak "Oak"). In the north, the taiga is a mixed [spruce](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spruce "Spruce") – [pine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pine "Pine") – [birch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birch "Birch") forest; further north within Russia and extreme northern Scandinavia, the taiga gives way to [tundra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra "Tundra") as the Arctic is approached. In the Mediterranean, many [olive](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olive "Olive") trees have been planted, which are very well adapted to its arid climate; [Mediterranean Cypress](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cupressus_sempervirens "Cupressus sempervirens") is also widely planted in southern Europe. The semi-arid Mediterranean region hosts much scrub forest. A narrow east–west tongue of Eurasian [grassland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grassland "Grassland") (the [steppe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steppe "Steppe")) extends westwards from [Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") and southern Russia and ends in Hungary and traverses into taiga to the north.

### Fauna

[Biogeographic regions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeography "Biogeography") of Europe and bordering regions

Glaciation during the [most recent ice age](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation "Quaternary glaciation") and the presence of humans affected the distribution of [European fauna](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna_of_Europe "Fauna of Europe"). As for the animals, in many parts of Europe most large animals and top [predator](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predator "Predator") species have been hunted to extinction. The [woolly mammoth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woolly_mammoth "Woolly mammoth") was extinct before the end of the [Neolithic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic "Neolithic") period. Today [wolves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf "Wolf") ([carnivores](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivore "Carnivore")) and [bears](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bear "Bear") ([omnivores](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivore "Omnivore")) are endangered. Once they were found in most parts of Europe. However, deforestation and hunting caused these animals to withdraw further and further. By the Middle Ages the bears' habitats were limited to more or less inaccessible mountains with sufficient forest cover. Today, the [brown bear](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_brown_bear "European brown bear") lives primarily in the [Balkan peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan "Balkan"), Scandinavia and Russia; a small number also persist in other countries across Europe (Austria, Pyrenees etc.), but in these areas brown bear populations are fragmented and marginalised because of the destruction of their habitat. In addition, [polar bears](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_bear "Polar bear") may be found on [Svalbard](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svalbard "Svalbard"), a Norwegian archipelago far north of Scandinavia. The [wolf](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_wolf "Eurasian wolf"), the second-largest predator in Europe after the brown bear, can be found primarily in [Central and Eastern Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe "Central and Eastern Europe") and in the Balkans, with a handful of packs in pockets of [Western Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe "Western Europe") (Scandinavia, Spain, etc.).

Once roaming the great temperate forests of Eurasia, [European bison](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_bison "European bison") now live in nature preserves in [Białowieża Forest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest "Białowieża Forest"), on the border between [Poland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland "Poland") and [Belarus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus").[^274] [^275]

Other carnivores include the [European wildcat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_wildcat "European wildcat"), [red fox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_fox "Red fox") and [arctic fox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_fox "Arctic fox"), the [golden jackal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_jackal "Golden jackal"), different species of [martens](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marten "Marten"), the [European hedgehog](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_hedgehog "European hedgehog"), different species of reptiles (like snakes such as vipers and grass snakes) and amphibians, as well as different birds ([owls](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Owl "Owl"), [hawks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawk "Hawk") and other birds of prey).

Important European herbivores are snails, larvae, fish, different birds and mammals, like rodents, deer and roe deer, boars and living in the mountains, marmots, steinbocks, chamois among others. A number of insects, such as the [small tortoiseshell](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_tortoiseshell "Small tortoiseshell") butterfly, add to the biodiversity.[^276]

Sea creatures are also an important part of European flora and fauna. The sea flora is mainly [phytoplankton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytoplankton "Phytoplankton"). Important animals that live in European seas are [zooplankton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zooplankton "Zooplankton"), [molluscs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mollusc "Mollusc"), [echinoderms](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echinoderm "Echinoderm"), different [crustaceans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crustacean "Crustacean"), [squids](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Squid "Squid") and [octopuses](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octopuses "Octopuses"), fish, [dolphins](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolphin "Dolphin") and [whales](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whales "Whales").

Biodiversity is protected in Europe through the Council of Europe's [Bern Convention](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_on_the_Conservation_of_European_Wildlife_and_Natural_Habitats "Convention on the Conservation of European Wildlife and Natural Habitats"), which has also been signed by the [European Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Community "European Community") as well as non-European states.

## Politics

The political map of Europe is substantially derived from the re-organisation of Europe following the [Napoleonic Wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars") in 1815. The prevalent form of government in Europe is [parliamentary democracy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy "Parliamentary democracy"), in most cases in the form of [republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic "Republic"); in 1815, the prevalent form of government was still the [monarchy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monarchies_in_Europe "Monarchies in Europe"). Europe's remaining eleven monarchies [^277] are [constitutional](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy "Constitutional monarchy").

[European integration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_integration "European integration") is the process of political, legal, economic (and in some cases social and cultural) integration of European states as it has been pursued by the powers sponsoring the [Council of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe") since the end of the [Second World War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_World_War "Second World War"). The [European Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") has been the focus of economic integration on the continent since its foundation in 1993. More recently, the [Eurasian Economic Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union "Eurasian Economic Union") has been established as a counterpart comprising former Soviet states.

27 European states are members of the politico-economic European Union, 26 of the border-free [Schengen Area](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schengen_Area "Schengen Area") and 20 of the monetary union [Eurozone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone"). Among the smaller European organisations are the [Nordic Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nordic_Council "Nordic Council"), the [Benelux](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benelux "Benelux"), the [Baltic Assembly](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Assembly "Baltic Assembly"), and the [Visegrád Group](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group "Visegrád Group").

The least [democratic countries in Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_in_Europe "Democracy in Europe") are [Belarus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus"), Russia, and [Turkey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") in 2024 according to the [V-Dem Democracy indices](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-Dem_Democracy_indices "V-Dem Democracy indices").[^278]

This list includes all internationally recognised sovereign countries falling even partially under any [common geographical or political definitions of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regions_of_Europe "Regions of Europe").

Within the above-mentioned states are several [de facto](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto "De facto") independent countries with [limited to no international recognition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition "List of states with limited recognition"). None of them are members of the UN:

Several dependencies and similar territories with broad autonomy are also found within or close to Europe. This includes [Åland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%85land "Åland") (an [autonomous county](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counties_of_Finland "Counties of Finland") of Finland), two [autonomous territories of the Kingdom of Denmark](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_Realm "Danish Realm") (other than Denmark proper), three [Crown Dependencies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Dependencies "Crown Dependencies") and two [British Overseas Territories](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories "British Overseas Territories"). [Svalbard](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svalbard "Svalbard") is also included due to its unique status within Norway, although it is not autonomous. Not included are the three [countries of the United Kingdom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom "Countries of the United Kingdom") with devolved powers and the two [Autonomous Regions of Portugal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_Regions_of_Portugal "Autonomous Regions of Portugal"), which despite having a unique degree of autonomy, are not largely self-governing in matters other than international affairs. Areas with little more than a unique tax status, such as the [Canary Islands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canary_Islands "Canary Islands") and [Heligoland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heligoland "Heligoland"), are also not included for this reason.

## Economy

GDP (PPP) per capita of European countries

| \| \>$60,000 \| $50,000 – $60,000 \| \| --- \| --- \| \| $40,000 – $50,000 \| $30,000 – $40,000 \| \| $20,000 – $30,000 \| $10,000 – $20,000 \| \|  \|  \| \|  \|  \| \|  \|  \| \|  \|  \| \|  \|  \| |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

As a continent, the economy of Europe is currently the largest on Earth and it is the richest region as measured by assets under management with over $32.7 trillion compared to North America's $27.1 trillion in 2008.[^281] In 2009 Europe remained the wealthiest region. Its $37.1 trillion in assets under management represented one-third of the world's wealth. It was one of several regions where wealth surpassed its precrisis year-end peak.[^282] As with other continents, Europe has a large [wealth gap](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_gap "Wealth gap") among its countries. The richer states tend to be in the [Northwest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwestern_Europe "Northwestern Europe") and [West](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Europe "Western Europe") in general, followed by [Central Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe"), while most economies of [Eastern](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe "Eastern Europe") and [Southeastern Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Europe "Southeastern Europe") are still reemerging from the [collapse of the Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Soviet_Union "Collapse of the Soviet Union") and the [breakup of Yugoslavia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia "Breakup of Yugoslavia").

The model of the [Blue Banana](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Banana "Blue Banana") was designed as an economic geographic representation of the respective economic power of the regions, which was further developed into the [Golden Banana](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Banana "Golden Banana") or Blue Star. The trade between East and West, as well as towards Asia, which had been disrupted for a long time by the two world wars, new borders and the Cold War, increased sharply after 1989. In addition, there is new impetus from the Chinese [Belt and Road Initiative](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belt_and_Road_Initiative "Belt and Road Initiative") across the [Suez Canal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal") towards Africa and Asia.[^283]

The European Union, a political entity composed of 27 European states, comprises the [largest single economic area](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") in the world. Nineteen EU [countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone") share the [euro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro "Euro") as a common currency. Four European countries rank in the top ten of the world's largest [national economies in GDP (PPP)](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(PPP\) "List of countries by GDP (PPP)"). This includes (ranks according to the [IMF](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund "International Monetary Fund")): Russia (4), Germany (6), France (9) and the United Kingdom (10).

Some European countries are much richer than others. The richest in terms of nominal GDP is [Monaco](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monaco "Monaco") with its US$185,829 per capita (2018) and the poorest is [Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") with its US$3,659 per capita (2019).[^284]

As a whole, Europe's GDP per capita is US$21,767 according to a 2016 International Monetary Fund assessment.[^285]
