### Economic history

Industrial growth (1760–1945)

Capitalism has been dominant in the Western world since the end of feudalism.[^288] From Britain, it gradually spread throughout Europe.[^289] The [Industrial Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution "Industrial Revolution") started in Europe, specifically the United Kingdom in the late 18th century,[^290] and the 19th century saw Western Europe industrialise. Economies were disrupted by the First World War, but by the beginning of the Second World War, they had recovered and were having to compete with the growing economic strength of the United States. The Second World War, again, damaged much of Europe's industries.

Cold War (1945–1991)

Fall of the [Berlin Wall](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_Wall "Berlin Wall") in 1989

[Eurozone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone") (blue colour)

After the Second World War the economy of the UK was in a state of ruin,[^291] and continued to suffer relative economic decline in the following decades.[^292] Italy was also in a poor economic condition but regained a high level of growth by the 1950s. West Germany [recovered quickly](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder "Wirtschaftswunder") and had doubled production from pre-war levels by the 1950s.[^293] France also staged a remarkable comeback enjoying rapid growth and modernisation; later on Spain, under the leadership of [Franco](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Franco "Francisco Franco"), also recovered and the nation recorded huge unprecedented economic growth beginning in the 1960s in what is called the [Spanish miracle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_miracle "Spanish miracle").[^294] The majority of [Central and Eastern European](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe "Central and Eastern Europe") states came under the control of the [Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") and thus were members of the [Council for Mutual Economic Assistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_for_Mutual_Economic_Assistance "Council for Mutual Economic Assistance") (COMECON).[^295]

The states which retained a [free-market](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free-market "Free-market") system were given a large amount of aid by the United States under the [Marshall Plan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Plan "Marshall Plan").[^296] The western states moved to link their economies together, providing the basis for the EU and increasing cross border trade. This helped them to enjoy rapidly improving economies, while those states in COMECON were struggling in a large part due to the cost of the [Cold War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"). Until 1990, the [European Community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Community "European Community") was expanded from 6 founding members to 12. The emphasis placed on resurrecting the West German economy led to it overtaking the UK as Europe's largest economy.

Reunification (1991–present)

One of [Kosovo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo") 's main economical sources is [mining](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mining "Mining"), because it has large reserves of lead, [zinc](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zinc "Zinc"), silver, [nickel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nickel "Nickel"), [cobalt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cobalt "Cobalt"), copper, iron and [bauxite](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bauxite "Bauxite").[^297] Miners at the [Trepča Mines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trep%C4%8Da_Mines "Trepča Mines") in [Mitrovica](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitrovica,_Kosovo "Mitrovica, Kosovo"), Kosovo in 2011.

With the fall of communism in Central and Eastern Europe in 1991, the post-socialist states underwent [shock therapy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shock_therapy_\(economics\) "Shock therapy (economics)") measures to liberalise their economies and implement free market reforms.

After [East](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") and West Germany were reunited in 1990, the economy of West Germany struggled as it had to support and largely rebuild the infrastructure of East Germany, while the latter [experienced sudden mass unemployment and plummeting of industrial production](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_German_reunification "Economic history of the German reunification").

By the millennium change, the EU dominated the economy of Europe, comprising the five largest European economies of the time: Germany, the United Kingdom, France, Italy, and Spain. In 1999, 12 of the 15 members of the EU joined the [Eurozone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurozone "Eurozone"), replacing their national currencies by the [euro](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euro "Euro").

Figures released by [Eurostat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurostat "Eurostat") in 2009 confirmed that the Eurozone had gone into [recession](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_2000s_recession_in_Europe "Late 2000s recession in Europe") in 2008.[^298] It affected much of the region.[^299] In 2010, fears of a [sovereign debt crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis "European sovereign-debt crisis") [^300] developed concerning some countries in Europe, especially Greece, Ireland, Spain and Portugal.[^301] As a result, measures were taken, especially for Greece, by the leading countries of the Eurozone.[^302] The [EU-27](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") unemployment rate was 10.3% in 2012. For those aged 15–24 it was 22.4%.[^303]

## Demographics

[Population growth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_growth "Population growth") in and around Europe in 2021 [^304]

The population of Europe was about 742 million in 2023 according to UN estimates.[^23] [^24] This is slightly more than one ninth of the world's population.<sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cnote_v">[v]</a></sup> The [population density](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_density "Population density") of Europe (the number of people per area) is the second highest of any continent, behind Asia. The population of Europe is currently slowly decreasing, by about 0.2% per year,[^305] because [there are fewer births than deaths](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility "Sub-replacement fertility"). This natural decrease in population is reduced by the fact that more people [migrate to Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_Europe "Immigration to Europe") from other continents than vice versa.

Southern Europe and Western Europe are the regions with the highest average number of elderly people in the world. In 2021, the percentage of people over 65 years old was 21% in Western Europe and Southern Europe, compared to 19% in all of Europe and 10% in the world.[^306] Projections suggest that by 2050 Europe will reach 30%.[^307] This is caused by the fact that the population has been [having children below replacement level](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_fertility_rate "Total fertility rate") since the 1970s. The [United Nations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") predicts that Europe will decline in population between 2022 and 2050 by −7 per cent, without changing immigration movements.[^308]

According to a population projection of the UN Population Division, Europe's population may fall to between 680 and 720 million people by 2050, which would be 7% of the world population at that time.[^309] Within this context, significant disparities exist between regions in relation to [fertility rates](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertility_rates "Fertility rates"). The average number of [children per female](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_fertility_rate "List of countries and territories by fertility rate") of child-bearing age is 1.52, far below the replacement rate.[^310] The UN predicts a steady [population decline](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_decline "Population decline") in [Central and Eastern Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe "Central and Eastern Europe") as a result of emigration and low birth rates.[^311]

### Ethnic groups

Pan and Pfeil (2004) count 87 distinct "peoples of Europe", of which 33 form the majority population in at least one sovereign state, while the remaining 54 constitute [ethnic minorities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_minority "Ethnic minority").[^312] [Romani people](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romani_people "Romani people") are the largest ethnic minority in Europe, according to [European Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission").[^313]

### Migration

Europe is home to the highest number of migrants of all global regions at nearly 87 million people in 2020, according to the [International Organisation for Migration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Organisation_for_Migration "International Organisation for Migration").[^314] In 2005, the EU had an overall net gain from [immigration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration "Immigration") of 1.8 million people. This accounted for almost 85% of Europe's total [population growth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_growth "Population growth").[^315] In 2021, 827,000 persons were given citizenship of an EU member state, an increase of about 14% compared with 2020.[^316] 2.3 million immigrants from non-EU countries entered the EU in 2021.[^316]

Early modern [emigration from Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emigration_from_Europe "Emigration from Europe") began with Spanish and Portuguese settlers in the 16th century,[^317] [^318] and French and English settlers in the 17th century.[^319] But numbers remained relatively small until waves of mass emigration in the 19th century, when millions of poor families left Europe.[^320]

Today, [large populations of European descent](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_diaspora "European diaspora") are found on every continent. European ancestry predominates in North America and to a lesser degree in South America (particularly in [Uruguay](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uruguay "Uruguay"), [Argentina](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina "Argentina"), [Chile](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chile "Chile") and [Brazil](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brazil "Brazil"), while most of the other [Latin American](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_America "Latin America") countries also have a considerable [population of European origins](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Latin_American "White Latin American")). Australia and New Zealand have large European-derived populations. Africa has no countries with European-derived majorities (or with the exception of [Cape Verde](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cape_Verde "Cape Verde") and probably [São Tomé and Príncipe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe "São Tomé and Príncipe"), depending on context), but there are significant minorities, such as the [White South Africans](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_South_Africans "White South Africans") in [South Africa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa"). In Asia, European-derived populations, specifically [Russians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russians "Russians"), predominate in [North Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Asia "North Asia") and some parts of Northern [Kazakhstan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan").[^321] Also in Asia, Europeans, especially the Spanish are an influential [minority population in the Philippines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Filipinos "Spanish Filipinos").[^322] [^323]

### Languages

Distribution of major [languages of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_Europe "Languages of Europe")

Europe has about 225 indigenous languages,[^324] mostly falling within three [Indo-European](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages") language groups: the [Romance languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romance_languages "Romance languages"), derived from the [Latin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_language "Latin language") of the [Roman Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"); the [Germanic languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_languages "Germanic languages"), whose ancestor language came from southern Scandinavia; and the [Slavic languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavic_languages "Slavic languages").<sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> Slavic languages are mostly spoken in Southern, Central and Eastern Europe. Romance languages are spoken primarily in Western and Southern Europe, as well as in [Switzerland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland") in Central Europe and [Romania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania "Romania") and [Moldova](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moldova "Moldova") in Eastern Europe. Germanic languages are spoken in Western, Northern and Central Europe as well as in [Gibraltar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibraltar "Gibraltar") and [Malta](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malta "Malta") in Southern Europe.<sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> Languages in adjacent areas show significant overlaps (such as in [English](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_\(language\) "English (language)"), for example). Other Indo-European languages outside the three main groups include the [Baltic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_languages "Baltic languages") group ([Latvian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvian_language "Latvian language") and [Lithuanian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuanian_language "Lithuanian language")), the [Celtic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtic_languages "Celtic languages") group ([Irish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_language "Irish language"), [Scottish Gaelic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic "Scottish Gaelic"), [Manx](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manx_language "Manx language"), [Welsh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welsh_language "Welsh language"), [Cornish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cornish_language "Cornish language") and [Breton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breton_language "Breton language") <sup><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup>), [Greek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language"), [Armenian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_language "Armenian language") and [Albanian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albanian_language "Albanian language").

A distinct non-Indo-European family of [Uralic languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uralic_languages "Uralic languages") ([Estonian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonian_language "Estonian language"), [Finnish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finnish_language "Finnish language"), [Hungarian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_language "Hungarian language"), [Erzya](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erzya_language "Erzya language"), [Komi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Komi_language "Komi language"), [Mari](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mari_language "Mari language"), [Moksha](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moksha_language "Moksha language") and [Udmurt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Udmurt_language "Udmurt language")) is spoken mainly in [Estonia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), [Finland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland "Finland"), [Hungary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungary "Hungary") and parts of Russia. [Turkic languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_languages "Turkic languages") include [Azerbaijani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijani_language "Azerbaijani language"), [Kazakh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakh_language "Kazakh language") and [Turkish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_language "Turkish language"), in addition to smaller languages in Eastern and Southeast Europe ([Balkan Gagauz Turkish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Gagauz_Turkish "Balkan Gagauz Turkish"), [Bashkir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashkir_language "Bashkir language"), [Chuvash](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuvash_language "Chuvash language"), [Crimean Tatar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language "Crimean Tatar language"), [Karachay-Balkar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karachay-Balkar_language "Karachay-Balkar language"), [Kumyk](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kumyk_language "Kumyk language"), [Nogai](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nogai_language "Nogai language") and [Tatar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatar_language "Tatar language")). [Kartvelian languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kartvelian_languages "Kartvelian languages") ([Georgian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgian_language "Georgian language"), [Mingrelian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mingrelian_language "Mingrelian language") and [Svan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svan_language "Svan language")) are spoken primarily in [Georgia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)"). Two other language families reside in the North Caucasus (termed [Northeast Caucasian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_Caucasian_languages "Northeast Caucasian languages"), most notably including [Chechen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chechen_language "Chechen language"), [Avar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avar_language "Avar language") and [Lezgin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lezgian_language "Lezgian language"); and [Northwest Caucasian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwest_Caucasian_languages "Northwest Caucasian languages"), most notably including [Adyghe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adyghe_language "Adyghe language")). [Maltese](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maltese_language "Maltese language") is the only [Semitic language](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semitic_language "Semitic language") that is official within the EU, while [Basque](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basque_language "Basque language") is the only European [language isolate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_isolate "Language isolate").

Multilingualism and the protection of regional and minority languages are recognised political goals in Europe today. The [Council of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe") [Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Framework_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_National_Minorities "Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities") and the Council of Europe's [European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages "European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages") set up a legal framework for language rights in Europe.

[Romani](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romani_language "Romani language") is spoken throughout Europe by the Roma minority.[^325]

### Religion

The largest religion in Europe is [Christianity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity"), with 76.2% of Europeans considering themselves [Christians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians "Christians"),[^326] [^327] including [Catholic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic "Catholic"), [Eastern Orthodox](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church") and various [Protestant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protestant "Protestant") denominations. Among Protestants, the most popular are [Lutheranism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutheranism "Lutheranism"), [Anglicanism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglicanism "Anglicanism") and the [Reformed faith](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reformed_faith "Reformed faith"). Smaller Protestant denominations include [Anabaptists](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anabaptists "Anabaptists") as well as denominations centred in the United States such as [Pentecostalism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentecostalism "Pentecostalism"), [Methodism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Methodism "Methodism"), and [Evangelicalism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evangelical_Protestants "Evangelical Protestants"). Although Christianity originated in the Middle East, its centre of mass shifted to Europe when it [became the official religion of the Roman Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_as_the_Roman_state_religion "Christianity as the Roman state religion") in the late 4th century. [Christianity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") played [a prominent role in the development](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization "Role of Christianity in civilization") of the [European culture](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_culture "European culture") and [identity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_identity "European identity").[^328] [^329] [^330] Today, just over 25% of the world's Christians live in Europe.[^331]

[Islam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") is the second most popular religion in Europe. Over 25 million, or roughly 5% of the population, adhere to it.[^332] In [Albania](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albania "Albania") and [Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Bosnia and Herzegovina"), two countries in the [Balkan peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_peninsula "Balkan peninsula") in Southeastern Europe, Islam instead of Christianity is the majority religion. This is also the case in [Turkey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") and in [certain parts of Russia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Russia "Islam in Russia"), as well as in [Azerbaijan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") and [Kazakhstan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan"), all of which are at the border to Asia.[^332] Many countries in Europe are home to a sizeable Muslim minority, and [immigration to Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_Europe "Immigration to Europe") has increased the number of Muslim people in Europe in recent years.

The [Jewish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism "Judaism") population in Europe was about 1.4 million people in 2020 (about 0.2% of the population).[^333] There is a long [history of Jewish life in Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Europe "History of the Jews in Europe"), beginning in antiquity. During the late 19th and early 20th centuries, the Russian Empire had the majority of the world's Jews living within its borders.[^334] In 1897, according to [Russian census of 1897](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census "Russian Empire Census"), the total Jewish population of Russia was 5.1 million people, which was 4.13% of total population. Of this total, the vast majority lived within the [Pale of Settlement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement "Pale of Settlement").[^335] In 1933, there were about 9.5 million Jewish people in Europe, representing 1.7% of the population,[^336] but most were killed, and most of the rest displaced, during [the Holocaust](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust").[^337] [^333] In the 21st century, [France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France") has the largest [Jewish population](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_population "Jewish population") in Europe, followed by the United Kingdom, [Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany") and Russia.[^29]

Other religions practiced in Europe include [Hinduism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism") and [Buddhism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), which are minority religions, except in Russia's [Republic of Kalmykia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Kalmykia "Republic of Kalmykia"), where Tibetan Buddhism is the majority religion.

A large and increasing number of people in Europe are [irreligious](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irreligion "Irreligion"), [atheist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atheism "Atheism") and [agnostic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agnosticism "Agnosticism"). They are estimated to make up about 18.3% of Europe's population currently.[^29]

The three largest [urban areas of Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_Europe "List of urban areas in Europe") are [Moscow](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow "Moscow"), [London](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/London "London") and [Paris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris "Paris"). All have over 10 million residents,[^338] and as such have been described as [megacities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megacity "Megacity").[^339] While [Istanbul](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul") has the highest total city population, it lies partly in [Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia"). 64.9% of the residents live on the European side and 35.1% on the Asian side. The next largest cities in order of population are [Madrid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrid "Madrid"), [Saint Petersburg](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg"), [Milan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan "Milan"), [Barcelona](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barcelona "Barcelona"), [Berlin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin "Berlin"), and [Rome](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome "Rome") each having over three million residents.[^338]

When considering the commuter belts or [metropolitan areas within Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe "List of metropolitan areas in Europe") (for which comparable data is available), Moscow covers the largest population, followed in order by Istanbul, London, Paris, Madrid, Milan, Ruhr Area, Saint Petersburg, Rhein-Süd, Barcelona and Berlin.[^340]

European [megacities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megacity "Megacity")

[Moscow](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow "Moscow")

[London](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/London "London")

[Paris](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris "Paris")

## Culture

Map purportedly displaying the European continent split along cultural and state borders as proposed by the German organisation [Ständiger Ausschuss für geographische Namen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_Committee_on_Geographical_Names_\(Germany\) "Permanent Committee on Geographical Names (Germany)") (StAGN)

"Europe" as a cultural concept is substantially derived from the shared heritage of [ancient Greece](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece") and the [Roman Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") and its cultures. The boundaries of Europe were historically understood as those of [Christendom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christendom "Christendom") (or more specifically [Latin Christendom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_Christendom "Latin Christendom")), as established or defended throughout the medieval and early modern history of Europe, especially [against Islam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests "Early Muslim conquests"), as in the [Reconquista](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconquista "Reconquista") and the [Ottoman wars in Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe "Ottoman wars in Europe").[^341]

This shared cultural heritage is combined by overlapping indigenous national cultures and folklores, roughly divided into [Slavic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavic_Europe "Slavic Europe"), [Latin (Romance)](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romance-speaking_Europe "Romance-speaking Europe") and Germanic, but with several components not part of either of these groups (notably [Greek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_culture "Greek culture"), [Basque](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basque_culture "Basque culture") and [Celtic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtic_Europe "Celtic Europe")). Historically, special examples with overlapping cultures are [Strasbourg](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strasbourg "Strasbourg") with Latin (Romance) and Germanic, or [Trieste](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trieste "Trieste") with Latin, Slavic and Germanic roots. Cultural contacts and mixtures shape a large part of the regional cultures of Europe. Europe is often described as "maximum cultural diversity with minimal geographical distances".

Different cultural events are organised in Europe, with the aim of bringing different cultures closer together and raising awareness of their importance, such as the [European Capital of Culture](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture "European Capital of Culture"), the [European Region of Gastronomy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Region_of_Gastronomy "European Region of Gastronomy"), the [European Youth Capital](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Youth_Capital "European Youth Capital") and the European Capital of Sport.

### Sport

Sport in Europe tends to be highly organised with many sports having professional leagues. The origins of many of the world's most popular sports today lie in the codification of many traditional games, especially in the United Kingdom. However, a paradoxical feature of European sport is the extent to which local, regional and national variations continue to exist, and even in some instances to predominate.[^342]

### Social dimension

In Europe many people are unable to access basic social conditions, which makes it harder for them to thrive and flourish. Access to basic necessities can be compromised, for example 10% of Europeans spend at least 40% of household income on housing. 75 million Europeans feel [socially isolated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_isolation "Social isolation"). From the 1980s income inequality has been rising and wage shares have been falling. In 2016, the richest 20% of households earned over five times more than the poorest 20%. Many workers experience stagnant [real wages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_wages "Real wages") and [precarious work](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precarious_work "Precarious work") is common even for [essential workers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Essential_workers "Essential workers").[^343]

[^2]: Russia is a [transcontinental country](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries "List of transcontinental countries") spanning Eastern Europe and [North Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Asia "North Asia"). The vast majority of its population (80%) lives within its [European part](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Russia "European Russia").[^344] However, only the population figure includes the entire state.

[^3]: [Guernsey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guernsey "Guernsey"), the [Isle of Man](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isle_of_Man "Isle of Man"), and [Jersey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jersey "Jersey") are [Crown Dependencies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_Dependencies "Crown Dependencies") of the United Kingdom. Other [Channel Islands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channel_Islands "Channel Islands") legislated by the [Bailiwick of Guernsey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey "Bailiwick of Guernsey") include [Alderney](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alderney "Alderney") and [Sark](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sark "Sark").

[^4]: [Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") can be considered part of Europe or [West Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"); it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe. The population and area figures refer to the entire state, including the *de facto* independent part [Northern Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Cyprus "Northern Cyprus") which is not recognised as a sovereign nation by the vast majority of sovereign nations, nor the UN.

[^5]: Figures for [Portugal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portugal "Portugal") include the [Azores](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azores "Azores") and [Madeira](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madeira "Madeira") archipelagos, both in the North Atlantic.

[^6]: Area figure for [Serbia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbia "Serbia") includes [Kosovo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo"), a province that unilaterally declared its independence from Serbia on 17 February 2008, and whose sovereign status is unclear. Population and density figures are from the first results of 2011 census and are given without the disputed territory of [Kosovo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo").

[^7]: Figures for [France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France") include only [metropolitan France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_France "Metropolitan France"): some [politically integral parts of France](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_France "Administrative divisions of France") are geographically located outside Europe.

[^8]: [Netherlands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands") population for November 2014. Population and area details include European portion only: Netherlands and three entities outside Europe ([Aruba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aruba "Aruba"), [Curaçao](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao "Curaçao"), and [Sint Maarten](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sint_Maarten "Sint Maarten"), in the [Caribbean](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean")) constitute the [Kingdom of the Netherlands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands "Kingdom of the Netherlands"). [Amsterdam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amsterdam "Amsterdam") is the official capital, while [The Hague](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hague "The Hague") is the administrative seat.

[^9]: [Kazakhstan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan") is physiographically considered a transcontinental country, mostly in Central Asia (UN region), partly in Eastern Europe, with European territory west of the [Ural Mountains](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ural_Mountains "Ural Mountains") and [Ural River](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ural_River "Ural River"). However, only the population figure refers to the entire country.

[^10]: [Armenia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia "Armenia") can be considered part of Eastern Europe or [West Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"); it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe. The population and area figures include the entire state, respectively.

[^11]: [Azerbaijan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") is physiographically considered a transcontinental country, mostly in Western Asia. A small portion of its territory is located north of [Greater Caucasus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greater_Caucasus "Greater Caucasus"), considered part of Eastern Europe.[^345] However the population and area figures are for the entire state. This includes the [exclave](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exclave "Exclave") of the [Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic "Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic") and the region [Nagorno-Karabakh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh "Nagorno-Karabakh").

[^12]: [Georgia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)") can be considered part of Eastern Europe or [West Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia");[^345] it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe.[^346] The population and area figures include Georgian estimates for [Abkhazia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abkhazia "Abkhazia") and [South Ossetia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ossetia "South Ossetia"), two regions that have declared and *[de facto](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* [achieved](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition "List of states with limited recognition") independence. [International recognition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia#Positions_taken_by_states "International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia"), however, is limited.

[^13]: [Turkey](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") is physiographically considered a transcontinental country, mostly in West Asia (the Middle East). Turkey has a small part of its territory (3%) in Southeast Europe called [East Thrace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Thrace "East Thrace").[^347] However, only the population figure includes the entire state.

[^14]: The total figures for area and population include only European portions of transcontinental countries. The precision of these figures is compromised by the ambiguous geographical extent of Europe and the lack of references for European portions of transcontinental countries.

[^15]: [Kosovo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo") unilaterally declared its independence from [Serbia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbia "Serbia") on 17 February 2008. Its sovereign status is [unclear](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence "International reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence"). Its population is July 2009 CIA estimate.

[^16]: [Abkhazia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abkhazia "Abkhazia") and [South Ossetia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ossetia "South Ossetia"), both of which can be considered part of Eastern Europe or [West Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia") [^345] unilaterally declared their independence from [Georgia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)") on 25 August 1990 and 28 November 1991, respectively. Their status as sovereign nations is [not recognised](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia "International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia") by a vast majority of sovereign nations, nor the UN. Population figures stated as of 2003 census and 2000 estimates, respectively.

[^17]: [Nagorno-Karabakh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh "Nagorno-Karabakh"), which can be considered part of Eastern Europe or [West Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"), unilaterally declared its independence from [Azerbaijan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") on 6 January 1992. Its status as a sovereign nation is not recognised by any sovereign nation, nor the UN. Population figures stated as of 2003 census and 2000 estimates, respectively.

[^18]: [Greenland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenland "Greenland"), an autonomous constituent country within the [Danish Realm](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danish_Realm "Danish Realm"), is geographically a part of the continent of North America, but has been politically and culturally associated with Europe.

[^19]: The [Donetsk People's Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donetsk_People%27s_Republic "Donetsk People's Republic") and [Luhansk People's Republic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luhansk_People%27s_Republic "Luhansk People's Republic") are internationally recognised as being a legal part of [Ukraine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine"), although *de facto* control is exercised by governments which declared independence from Ukraine in 2014.

[^20]: Europe is normally considered its own continent in the English-speaking world, which uses the seven continent model.[^348] [^349] Other models consider Europe as part of a Eurasian or Afro-Eurasian continent. See [Continent § Number](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continent#Number "Continent") for more information.

[^21]: The map shows one of the most commonly accepted delineations of the geographical boundaries of Europe, as used by [National Geographic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Geographic_Society "National Geographic Society") and [Encyclopædia Britannica](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica "Encyclopædia Britannica"). Whether countries are considered in Europe or Asia can vary in sources, for example in the classification of the [CIA World Factbook](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook "CIA World Factbook") or that of the [BBC](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC "BBC"). Certain countries in Europe, such as France, have [territories lying geographically outside Europe](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_spanning_more_than_one_continent#Non-contiguous "List of countries spanning more than one continent"), but which are nevertheless considered integral parts of that country.

[^323]: Go MC, Jones AR, Algee-Hewitt B, Dudzik B, Hughes C (2019). ["Classification Trends among Contemporary Filipino Crania Using Fordisc 3.1"](https://www.academia.edu/38744342). *Human Biology*. **2** (4). University of Florida Press: 293– 303. [doi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.5744/fa.2019.1005](https://doi.org/10.5744%2Ffa.2019.1005). [S2CID](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2CID_\(identifier\) "S2CID (identifier)") [159266278](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:159266278). [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20210107133718/https://www.academia.edu/38744342/Classification_Trends_Among_Modern_Filipino_Crania_Using_Fordisc_3_1) from the original on 7 January 2021. Retrieved 13 September 2020. \[Page 1\] ABSTRACT: Filipinos represent a significant contemporary demographic group globally, yet they are underrepresented in the forensic anthropological literature. Given the complex population history of the Philippines, it is important to ensure that traditional methods for assessing the biological profile are appropriate when applied to these peoples. Here we analyze the classification trends of a modern Filipino sample (n = 110) when using the Fordisc 3.1 (FD3) software. We hypothesize that Filipinos represent an admixed population drawn largely from Asian and marginally from European parental gene pools, such that FD3 will classify these individuals morphometrically into reference samples that reflect a range of European admixture, in quantities from small to large. Our results show the greatest classification into Asian reference groups (72.7%), followed by Hispanic (12.7%), Indigenous American (7.3%), African (4.5%), and European (2.7%) groups included in FD3. This general pattern did not change between males and females. Moreover, replacing the raw craniometric values with their shape variables did not significantly alter the trends already observed. These classification trends for Filipino crania provide useful information for casework interpretation in forensic laboratory practice. Our findings can help biological anthropologists to better understand the evolutionary, population historical, and statistical reasons for FD3-generated classifications. The results of our studyindicate that ancestry estimation in forensic anthropology would benefit from population-focused research that gives consideration to histories of colonialism and periods of admixture.
